Fourth Proof: God's Power Over the Servant's Action Through Motion
The author uses the example of moving a body to show that God and servant share the same object of power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the example of moving a body from one location to another demonstrates that God is powerful over the servant's action, and why the motion must be the same object of power for both.

Core Idea
The same motion cannot be distinct in non-existence; thus God and servant share its power.

This lesson presents Sanusi's fourth proof for God's power over human actions. Using the concrete example of moving a body from one location to another, he shows that unless the servant's action is also under God's power, absurd consequences follow. You will follow the logical steps and see why the motion must be the same object of power for both.

Guided Path
1
Understand the setup
Read the opening sentence: 'There is no doubt that He Most High is powerful over moving that body... Also, the servant is powerful over it.' Notice that both God and servant are said to be capable of moving the same body.
The body and the motion are hypothetical; the focus is on logical possibility.
2
Follow the conditional argument
Trace the conditional reasoning: If the servant's object of power were not also God's, then the transition caused by the servant would be distinct from the transition caused by God before existence. But distinguishing them requires a difference in their realities, which is impossible for non-existent entities.
The key phrase is 'before entrance into existence' – the argument deals with logical prior states, not temporal ones.
3
Analyze the two reasons for impossibility
Study the two reasons given: (1) It would make non-existence a thing, which is absurd. (2) The body's being in a location has no reality except as a relation that cannot hold for a non-existent body. Understand how these reasons block the distinction.
The second reason is more subtle: the motion is merely a relation ('being in a location') that cannot be realized without a subject.
4
Conclude the proof
The absurd conclusion shows that the two motions cannot be distinct; therefore they must be the same. Thus, the servant's action is under God's power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : لا شك أنه تعالى قادر على نقل ذلك الجسم ، من ذلك الحيز إلى الحيز الثاني . وأيضاً : العبد قادر عليه . فلو لم يكن مقدور العبد مقدوراً الله تعالى ، لكان ذلك الانتقال ، الذي حصل بقدرة العبد : مميزاً عن ذلك الانتقال الذي حصل بفعل الله تعالى ، قبل دخولهما في الوجود . لأنه قبل دخولهما في الوجود ، صدق على أحدهما أنه يجب أن يكون مقدوراً الله تعالى ، ويمتنع أن يكون مقدوراً للعبد ، وصدق على الثاني أنه يجب أن يكون مقدوراً للعبد ، ويمتنع أن يكون مقدوراً الله تعالى . والتباين باللوازم والصفات ، موقوف على التباين بالحقائق والماهيات. فثبت : أنه لو لم يكن مقدور العبد ، مقدوراً الله تعالى ، لوجب أن يكون الانتقال الذي هو مقدور للعبد ، مميزاً عن الانتقال الذي هو مقدور الله تعالى ، قبل الدخول في الوجود . إلا أن هذا محال لوجهين : الأول : إنه يلزم منه كون المعدوم شيئاً ، وهو محال . والثاني : حصول الجسم في الحيز لا حقيقة له ، ولا ماهية له إلا هذا الحصول ، وتحقق هذا الحصول حال كون الجسم معدوماً : محال . إلا أن يقال : الجسم حال عدمه حاصل في الحيز ، ومنتقل من حيز إلى حيز آخر . إلا أن هذا لا يقوله عاقل . ولو جاز ذلك ، فكيف الأمان من كون هذه المتحركات والساكنات معدومة ؟ ومعلوم أن من جوز ذلك ، فهو قد فارق العقل بالكلية.
The fourth proof: There is no doubt that He Most High is powerful over moving that body from that location to the second location. Also, the servant is powerful over it. So if the servant's object of power were not an object of power of God Most High, then that transition which occurred by the servant's power would be distinct from that transition which occurred by the act of God Most High, before their entry into existence. Because before their entry into existence, it is true of one of them that it must be an object of power of God Most High and impossible to be an object of power of the servant, and it is true of the second that it must be an object of power of the servant and impossible to be an object of power of God Most High. And differentiation by concomitants and attributes depends on differentiation by realities and quiddities. So it is established: if the servant's object of power were not an object of power of God Most High, then the transition which is an object of power of the servant would necessarily be distinct from the transition which is an object of power of God Most High, before entry into existence. However, this is impossible for two reasons: First, it would entail non-existence being a thing, which is impossible. Second, the body's being in a location has no reality and no quiddity except this 'being in a location', and the realization of this 'being in a location' while the body is non-existent is impossible. Unless it is said: the body while non-existent is in a location and moves from one location to another. But no rational person would say this. And if that were permissible, how could one be safe from these moving and stationary things being non-existent? It is known that whoever permits that has completely departed from reason.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof (al-hujja al-rabi'a). The author takes a concrete example: a body being moved from one location to another. Both God and the servant are capable of causing that motion. If the servant's object of power (the motion) were not also an object of God's power, then before either motion exists, there would be two distinct entities: one that must be God's power alone and the other that must be the servant's power alone. Distinguishing between them before existence requires a distinction in their realities or quiddities. But the motion is the same in terms of its reality; there is no quiddity for non-existent motion. Therefore, such a distinction is impossible. The author offers two reasons: (1) it would make non-existence a thing, which is absurd; (2) the body's being in a location has no reality except as a relation, and that relation cannot be realized while the body is non-existent. The absurd conclusion is that the servant's motion and God's motion would have to be different things in non-existence, which is impossible. Hence, they must be the same motion, proving that God is powerful over the servant's action.

الانتقال

الماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking the argument relies on God and servant both bringing about the same motion simultaneously.
Correction: The proof focuses on the logical properties of the motion before existence, not on concurrent causation.

Checkpoint
What is the first reason given for the impossibility of distinguishing the two transitions before existence?
A) It would require the body to have a quiddity.
B) It would entail that non-existence is something (a thing).
C) It would imply God cannot move bodies.
D) It would make the servant's power unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
God's power encompasses all actions, including those of the servant, because a single motion cannot have two distinct nonexistent realities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?

Does this change how you think about your intentions before you act? Are your intentions truly yours, or are they also under God's power? How does that reshape your reliance on Him?

The Objects of Divine and Human Power Have No Pre-Existence
Refutes the claim that the objects of God's power and human power are distinct by showing they have no pre-existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument showing that objects of divine and human power cannot be distinct because they have no pre-existence.

Core Idea
Without pre-existence, no distinction between objects of power is possible.

This passage tackles a key debate in Islamic theology: are the objects of God's power and human power distinct? The author presents a logical dilemma: either these objects exist before the act of power or not. By eliminating the first option, he shows that distinguishing them is impossible. The argument also refutes the idea of things subsisting in non-existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the logical flow: a dichotomy, a proof, and a response to an objection.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the initial dichotomy
The passage begins by stating two possibilities for the objects of power: either they have a pre-existence or they do not. Identify why the first option is impossible according to the definition of 'object of power'.
Focus on the definition: an object of power is realized by the agent's effect.
3
Follow the conclusion and objection
After establishing that no pre-existence exists, the passage concludes that distinguishing between objects of power is baseless. Then it considers an objection about things subsisting in non-existence and refutes it.
The objection is a common counterargument; see how it is dismantled.
4
Grasp the overall argument
Put together the pieces: the argument shows that since neither object of power has pre-existence, they cannot be separate. Thus, the servant's act is also under God's power.
This undermines any claim of independent human power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدورة الله تعالى . إما أن يكون لهما تحقق وتعين قبل الدخول في الوجود ، أو لا يكون . والأول محال . لأنه لا معنى للمقدور إلا الذي يكون تحققه وتكونه يقع بتأثير القادر. وما كان كذلك، كان تحققه متأخراً عن تأثير قدرة القادر ، والمتأخر عن تأثير القادر ممتنع أن يكون هو بعينه مقدماً على تأثير القادر . فثبت : أن الذي هو مقدور للعبد ، والذي هو مقدور الله تعالى : لا تحقق له ، ولا تعين له ، قبل الدخول في الوجود . وما كان كذلك ، امتنع أن يقع فيه الامتياز ، وكل ما لا امتياز فيه امتنع أن يقال : إن شيئاً منه مقدور للعبد ولا الله ، وشيء آخر منه مقدور الله ولا للعبد . فثبت : أن القول بأن مقدور العبد غير مقدور الله : يفضي إلى هذين القسمين الباطلين ، فيكون باطلاً بهذا الطريق . ومعنى قول من يقول : إن تلك المقدورات أشياء وأمور حاصلة في العدم ، أنا نقول : إن بتقدير أن يتحقق في العدم شيء أمور متميزة . إلا أن على هذا التقدير ، يمتنع كونها مقدورة . لأن المقدور هو الذي يكون تحققه ووقوعه ، لأجل تأثير القادر فيه . وما كان متحققاً في العدم ، يمتنع أن يقال : إن تحققه وتعينه لأجل تأثير القادر فيه . فثبت : أن ما كان مقدوراً ، يمتنع كونه متحققاً في العدم. وهذا كلام معتقد متين في تقرير هذا المطلوب
The objects of God's power. Either they have realization and determination before entering existence, or they do not. The first is impossible. Because there is no meaning of 'object of power' except that its realization and occurrence happen by the effect of the powerful agent. And whatever is like that, its realization is posterior to the effect of the power of the powerful agent, and that which is posterior to the effect of the powerful agent is impossible to be identical to what is prior to the effect of the powerful agent. So it is established that that which is an object of power for the servant and that which is an object of power for God Almighty have no realization and no determination before entering existence. And whatever is like that, it is impossible that differentiation occurs in it, and everything in which there is no differentiation, it is impossible to say: 'Some of it is an object of power for the servant and not for God, and another part of it is an object of power for God and not for the servant.' So it is established that the statement that the object of power of the servant is other than the object of power of God leads to these two false divisions, thus it is false by this path. And the meaning of the statement of one who says: 'Those objects of power are things and matters subsisting in non-existence' – we say: If we suppose that in non-existence there are things, distinct matters, except that on this supposition, it is impossible for them to be objects of power. Because the object of power is that whose realization and occurrence are due to the effect of the powerful agent in it. And whatever is subsisting in non-existence, it is impossible to say: 'Its realization and determination are due to the effect of the powerful agent in it.' So it is established that whatever is an object of power, it is impossible for it to be subsisting in non-existence. And this is sound creedal speech in establishing this sought conclusion.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the view that the objects of God's power and the objects of human power are distinct. The author begins by presenting a dichotomy: either these objects have realization and determination before they come into existence, or they do not. The first option is impossible because an object of power is defined as something that becomes realized through the effect of the powerful agent; therefore its realization must be posterior to that effect. If it were prior, it would contradict the definition. Thus, both the servant's object of power and God's object of power have no pre-existence. Since they lack pre-existence, there is no basis for distinguishing between them—one cannot say that some part belongs exclusively to the servant and another to God. Hence, affirming such a distinction leads to false conclusions. The author then addresses an objection: what if one claims that these objects are 'things' or 'matters' subsisting in non-existence? The author replies that even if we grant that there are distinct things in non-existence, they cannot be objects of power because an object of power is precisely that which is brought into existence by the agent. If they already subsist in non-existence, their realization is not due to the agent's effect. Therefore, anything that is an object of power cannot be pre-existing in non-existence. This argument establishes that the objects of power are not distinct; rather, they are identical, so the servant's act is also under God's power.

Key Terms
مقدور
تحقق
تعين
قادر
تأثير
امتياز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God's power and human power both act, their objects must be distinct.
Correction: The argument shows that lack of pre-existence prevents any distinction; both objects are identical in that they are brought into existence only by the agent's effect.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, why is it impossible for the objects of God's power and human power to be distinct?
A) Because they are both created by God
B) Because they have no realization or determination before existence, so there is no basis for distinction
C) Because human power does not actually produce any effect
D) Because God's power encompasses everything

Key Takeaway
The objects of divine and human power cannot be distinct because neither has any pre-existence, making differentiation impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every action you perform—even the turning of your thoughts—is also an act of God's power? How does that challenge your pride in your own achievements?
?
If your past mistakes have no independent existence apart from God's creation, are they solely yours to regret, or is your regret itself a sign of God's mercy? What does that mean for how you approach repentance?
?
How would your daily routine change if you constantly reminded yourself that the very ability to raise your hand is a direct effect of God's power at that instant? Does this thought unsettle you or liberate you from the burden of self-reliance?

The Sixth Proof: God's Power Over the Servant's Act
Sanusi presents the sixth proof that God is powerful over the servant's act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical reasoning behind the sixth proof that God is powerful over the servant's act, based on the principle that the one who empowers another must himself be powerful.

Core Idea
Empowerment implies the empowerer's own power over the very thing he empowers.

This lesson presents the sixth rational proof for God's power over human actions. The argument is tightly reasoned: it starts from an agreed premise—that God grants the servant ability to act—and then draws a necessary conclusion based on a logical principle. By the end, you will see why the empowerer must be powerful over the empowered act.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the structure: statement, premise, analogy, conclusion.
2
Identify the premise and conclusion
Note the agreed premise (God empowers the servant) and the conclusion (God is powerful over the servant's act).
The conclusion is derived from a general principle.
3
Examine the supporting analogy
The analogy compares empowerment to knowledge: as an ignorant person cannot make another knowledgeable, an incapable person cannot make another capable.
This analogy reinforces the principle.
4
Understand the logical necessity
Grasp why the conclusion necessarily follows: if the premise and principle are accepted, the conclusion is inescapable.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this proof supports the doctrine that God's power encompasses all acts, even those performed by servants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : إنه تعالى هو الذي أقدر العبد على الفعل . ومن أقدر غيره على شيء ، وجب أن يكون هو قادراً عليه . لأن العاجز عن الشيء ، يمتنع أن يجعل غيره قادراً عليه ، كما أن الجاهل بالشيء يمتنع أن يجعل غيره عالماً بذلك الشيء . ولما توافقنا على أن الله تعالى هو الذي أقدر العبد على الفعل وثبت : أن من أقدر غيره على فعل ، وجب أن يكون قادرا عليه : لزم القطع بكون الله تعالى قادرا على مقدور العبد
The sixth proof: He, exalted, is the one who empowered the servant over the act. And whoever makes another powerful over something, it is necessary that he himself be powerful over it, because the one incapable of a thing is unable to make another capable of it, just as the ignorant of a thing is unable to make another knowledgeable of that thing. And since we have agreed that God Almighty is the one who empowered the servant over the act, and it is established that whoever makes another powerful over an act must be powerful over it, it necessarily follows that God Almighty is powerful over the object of power of the servant.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is a proof (al-ḥujja al-sādisa) that God is powerful over the very act that the servant performs. The reasoning is straightforward: (1) God is the one who gives the servant power to act (a premise both parties accept). (2) If someone gives another power over something, that giver must himself be powerful over that thing. The author supports this by analogy: a person who is himself incapable of something cannot confer capability for it, just as an ignorant person cannot confer knowledge. (3) Therefore, since God grants the servant power over the act, God must Himself be powerful over that same act. The conclusion is that God is powerful over the object of the servant's power, meaning the servant's act is also under God's power.

Key Terms

قادر
مقدور
العبد
الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that empowerment does not imply the empowerer's power over the same act.
Correction: The argument shows it is necessary by analogy: an incapable person cannot confer capability, so the empowerer must be capable.

Checkpoint
What is the key analogy used in the sixth proof?
A) A rich person can make another rich
B) A person incapable of something cannot make another capable of it, just as an ignorant person cannot make another knowledgeable
C) A powerful person can delegate power
D) A creator must be greater than his creation

Key Takeaway
God's empowerment of the servant necessarily entails that God is powerful over the act itself.

?
In moments of pride or self-sufficiency, do you unconsciously deny this proof? What practical step can you take today to remind yourself that your power to act is a gift from the One who is truly powerful?

The Seventh Proof: God's Power Encompasses All Acts
Seventh proof: a fortiori argument from perfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the a fortiori argument (qiyās al-awlā) used to prove that God's perfect power necessarily applies to every act the servant performs.

Core Idea
If a weaker power can do it, a perfect power surely can.

This passage presents a concise yet powerful argument from perfection. The author argues that if the servant's deficient power can relate to an act, then God's perfect power is even more worthy of relating to it. This logical move, called a fortiori (awlā), is a staple of kalām reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage aloud
Read the Arabic once to get the rhythm. Notice the key terms: قادرية, أكمل, ناقصة, تعلق, أولى.
This is a short proof, so read carefully.
2
Identify the two premises
The argument has two premises: (1) God's power is more perfect than the servant's. (2) The servant's power can attach to the act. Then the conclusion follows by priority.
3
Understand the a fortiori principle
This is a logical principle: if a lesser thing has a property, then a greater thing has it even more. Here, if deficient power can relate, perfect power can relate even more.
This principle is used in many kalām proofs.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
The proof shows that God's power is not excluded from the servant's act. It affirms divine omnipotence without negating human agency.
The proof does not deny the servant's power; it subordinates it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : قادرية الله تعالى ، أكمل من قادرية العبد ، فإذا لم يمتنع تعلق قادرية العبد بذلك المقدور ، مع كون تلك القادرية ناقصة ، فبأن لا يمتنع ذلك في قادرية الله تعالى ، مع كونها كاملة ، كان أولى
The seventh proof: The power of God Almighty is more perfect than the power of the servant. So if it is not impossible for the power of the servant to be attached to that object of power, despite that power being deficient, then it is even more fitting that it is not impossible for the power of God Almighty, with it being perfect, to be attached to it.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is the seventh proof (al-ḥujja al-sābiʿa) that God's power is related to the act that the servant performs. It is an argument from perfection: (1) God's power is more perfect (akmal) than the servant's power. (2) The servant's power, despite being deficient (nāqiṣa), is still related to a certain act—it is not impossible for it to attach to that act. (3) Therefore, a fortiori (awlā), it should not be impossible for God's perfect power to also attach to that same act. The reasoning is that if a lesser power can relate to something, a greater power is even more able to relate to it. Thus, the servant's act is also under God's power.

Key Terms
قادرية
أكمل
ناقصة
تعلق
أولى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's power is too perfect to be concerned with human actions, or that human acts are exclusively under human control.
Correction: The a fortiori argument shows that if a lesser power can relate to an act, then a perfect power must also relate to it. God's perfection does not exclude involvement; rather, it entails it.

Checkpoint
What is the logical principle used in the seventh proof?
A) If a lesser power can do something, a greater power can also do it
B) If a power is perfect, it cannot be related to imperfect acts
C) The servant's power is independent
D) God's power is only over creation, not over human acts

Key Takeaway
God's perfect power necessarily relates to every human act because even deficient power can relate to it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If God's power is perfect and encompasses your acts, then what room is left for pride in your own achievements? How can you cultivate gratitude for even your ability to act?
?
Consider a sin you committed. Did you think at that moment that your power was separate from God's? How does this proof challenge that assumption and what does it demand of your repentance?

The Eighth Proof: God's Power Includes Human Acts
Eighth proof: reductio ad absurdum for divine power over human acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the eighth proof that God's power encompasses human acts, and why denying this leads to the absurd conclusion that God's power is limited.

Core Idea
To deny God's power over human acts is to limit the infinite.

This lesson presents the eighth proof from the author's series demonstrating that human acts fall under God's power. The argument uses a reductio ad absurdum: if human acts were outside God's power, then God's power would be smaller than the combined power of God and humans, implying finiteness. Since God's power is infinite, the assumption must be false.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the logical structure: assumption, comparison, conclusion.
Pay attention to the term 'mutaqawwimāt' (objects of power).
2
Identify the assumption and its necessary consequent
The proof assumes that human acts are not under God's power. From this, it derives that God's power would be finite. Trace this logical step.
The key move is comparing the set of God's power objects with and without human acts.
3
Grasp the set-theoretic reasoning
The proof states that the set of God's power objects (excluding human acts) is smaller than the full set including human acts. Anything smaller than another is finite.
This relies on the idea that infinite sets cannot be properly smaller than each other.
4
Understand why the consequent is false
God's power is infinite, so it cannot be finite. The proof labels this consequent as 'false' (bāṭil).
This is a standard reductio: false consequent implies false antecedent.
5
Appreciate the proof's role in the series
The author notes that this and the previous two proofs contain 'ījāb' (affirmation) – they positively establish the point, not merely refute objections.
Consider how this proof strengthens the overall argument for divine omnipotence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثامنة : لو لم يكن مقدور العبد ، مقدوراً الله تعالى . لزم تناهي مقدورات الله تعالى . لأن جملة مقدورات الله تعالى ، بهون مقدورات العباد : أقل من مجموع مقدورات الله تعالى مع مقدورات العباد . وكل ما كان أقل من غيره كان متناهياً . فلو لم تكن مقدورات العباد ، مقدورة الله تعالى . لزم أن يقال : مقدورات الله تعالى متناهية . ولما كان اللازم باطلاً ، كان الملزوم أيضاً باطلاً . وهذه الوجوه الثلاثة الأخيرة فيها إيجاب
The eighth proof: If the object of power of the servant were not an object of power of God Almighty, it would necessitate the limitation (finiteness) of the objects of power of God Almighty. Because the total of the objects of power of God Almighty, with the objects of power of the servants, is less than the sum of the objects of power of God Almighty together with the objects of power of the servants. And everything that is less than another is finite. So if the objects of power of the servants were not objects of power of God Almighty, it would necessitate that it be said: The objects of power of God Almighty are finite. And since the consequent is false, the antecedent is also false. And these last three proofs contain affirmation.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is the eighth proof (al-ḥujja al-thāmina) that the servant's act is under God's power. It is a reductio ad absurdum: (1) Assume that the object of the servant's power is not an object of God's power. (2) Then the set of God's objects of power (excluding the servant's acts) is smaller than the union of that set with the set of the servant's objects of power. (3) Anything that is smaller than something else is finite (because if it were infinite, it could not be smaller than another infinite). (4) Therefore, God's objects of power would be finite. (5) But God's power is infinite, so finiteness is false. (6) Hence, the assumption is false, and the servant's act must be under God's power. The author notes that these last three proofs (sixth, seventh, eighth) contain 'ījāb' (affirmation) — meaning they positively prove the point rather than being negative refutations.

Key Terms
تناهي
متناهية
مقدورات
أقل
مجموع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's power does not need to include human acts because humans have free will.
Correction: This proof shows that excluding human acts from God's power would imply finiteness of God's power, which is absurd. Therefore, free will must be compatible with divine omnipotence.

Checkpoint
What is the false consequent that is derived in the eighth proof?
A) God's power is imperfect
B) The servant's power is independent
C) God's objects of power are finite
D) Human acts are not created

Key Takeaway
God's power encompasses all things, including human acts, because otherwise His power would be finite, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that even that act is under God's power? How does that change your attitude towards repentance and reliance on His mercy?
?
If you genuinely internalized that every single action of yours — good or bad — is an object of God's power, would you live more humbly or more recklessly? What specific habit would change today?
?
The proof shows that denying God's power over your choices is absurd. Yet, in your heart, do you sometimes act as if your decisions are independent of Him? What would it take to surrender that illusion completely?

The Second Premise: First Proof of Divine Exclusivity in Causation
Sanusi presents the second premise and the first proof via a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second premise of the argument and the first proof that whatever is under God's power occurs only by His power, including the dilemma about two independent powers.

Core Idea
Two independent powers cannot produce a single act without preference.

This passage introduces a crucial premise and the first of two proofs for it. The argument uses a dilemma: if both God and the servant intend the same act, either it occurs or not. The proof shows that if it occurs, it cannot be by one power alone because there is no preference between two independent powers. This reasoning sets the stage for the Ashʿari position on causality.

Guided Path
1
Read the premise statement
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author states the second premise clearly: whatever is under God's power must occur by His power.
The premise is the conclusion the proof aims to establish.
2
Understand the dilemma
The author sets up a dilemma: if both the servant and God intend the same act, either the act occurs or it does not. Both alternatives are shown to be impossible, forcing a conclusion.
Focus on why 'does not occur' is impossible—it contradicts God's intention.
3
See why occurrence by one power is impossible
If the act occurs, it must be by one power or both. The author argues it cannot be by one because each power is independent, and there is no reason (preference) for one over the other.
This is key: independence eliminates any basis for selection.
4
Consider the objection and reply
The objection that God's power is stronger is raised and rebutted. The act is a single substance in a single time; it does not admit of degrees, so a stronger power cannot be the sole cause.
This reply reinforces the Ashʿari denial of secondary causality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المقدمة الثانية : فهي في بيان أن كل ما كان مقدوراً الله تعالى ، فعند وقوعه يجب أن يكون وقوعه بقدرة الله تعالى . وتقريره من وجهين : الأول : إن العبد إذا قصد إلى إيجاد مقدوره ، والله تعالى أيضاً قصد إلى إيجاده في ذلك الوقت. فإما أن يقع ذلك الفعل أو لا يقع . والقسمان باطلان ، فما أدى إليه يكون باطلاً . إنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع وقوعه . لأنه لو وقع . لوقع إما بإحدى القدرتين ، وإما بكل واحدة منهما . لا يجوز أن يقع بإحدى القدرتين ، لأن كل واحدة من هاتين القدرتين، لما فرضنا كونها مستقلة بالإيجاد ، لم يكن وقوع هذا الفعل بإحدى هاتين القدرتين أولى من وقوعه بالثانية . لا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن قدرة الله تعالى ، أقوى من قدرة العبد . فكان وقوع ذلك المقدور بقدرة الله تعالى أولى ؟ لأنا نقول : حصول الجوهر الواحد ، في الحيز الواحد ، في الزمان الواحد ، لا يقبل الأشد
And as for the second premise: it is an exposition that whatever is an object of power of God Almighty, at its occurrence its occurrence must be by the power of God Almighty. And its formulation is from two aspects: The first: If the servant intends to bring about his object of power, and God Almighty also intends to bring it about at that time, then either that act occurs or it does not occur. And both divisions are false, so what leads to them is false. We said: Indeed, its occurrence is impossible. Because if it occurred, it would occur either by one of the two powers, or by both of them. It is not permissible for it to occur by one of the two powers, because each of these two powers, since we have supposed them to be independent in bringing about, the occurrence of this act by one of these two powers would not be more preferable than its occurrence by the second. It cannot be said: Why is it not permissible to say that the power of God Almighty is stronger than the power of the servant, so the occurrence of that object of power by the power of God Almighty is more preferable? Because we say: The occurrence of a single substance in a single location in a single time does not admit of greater or lesser [intensity].
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage introduces the second premise (al-muqaddima al-thāniya) of a larger argument. The premise is: Whenever something is under God's power, when it occurs, it must occur by God's power alone (not by any other power). The author gives two proofs, but only the first is provided here. The first proof is a dilemma: Suppose both the servant and God intend to bring about the same act at the same time. Either the act occurs or it does not. If it does not occur, that contradicts the intention of both (especially God's). But if it occurs, it must occur by one of the two powers or by both. It cannot occur by one power because, given that both powers are supposed to be fully capable and independent, there is no reason for one to prevail over the other—no preference (awlā). It also cannot occur by both powers because a single act (a single substance in a single place at a single time) cannot be produced by two independent agents; it does not admit of degrees of intensity (al-ashadd) that would allow distribution. Therefore, the only possibility is that the act occurs solely by God's power, as the servant's power is not truly effective independently. The argument thus proves that the servant's act, when it occurs, is brought about by God's power alone.

Key Terms
المقدمة الثانية
قصد
إيجاد
قدرة
استقلال
الأشد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Both God and the servant can be independent causes of the same act, with one being stronger.
Correction: The argument shows that two independent powers cannot produce one unified act; the stronger power would still need preference, which is absent, and the act itself is indivisible.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof of the second premise, why can the act not occur by the power of the servant alone?
A) Because the servant's power is dependent on God
B) Because there would be no preference between the two independent powers
C) Because God's power is stronger
D) Because the act is impossible

Key Takeaway
The first proof of the second premise demonstrates that if two independent powers intend the same act, the act cannot be attributed to one without preference, so it must be solely by God's power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something you worked hard for, do you genuinely feel that it was entirely God's creation, or does a part of you think your effort was the decisive factor? What would it cost you to completely attribute every success to God alone?
?
The argument shows that two independent powers cannot produce a single act. How does this confront your everyday experience of feeling like you are the independent cause of your choices? Are you willing to let go of that feeling and submit to God's exclusive causation, even when it is uncomfortable?
?
If you truly believed that every breath you take is brought into existence directly by God at every moment, with no independent power of your own, what would change about how you plan your day? Would you still worry about the future, or would you trust God's power completely? Be honest.

Fourth Proof: Creator Must Know His Creation
Sanusi presents the fourth proof that the servant cannot be the creator of his actions due to ignorance of details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that a servant cannot be the creator of his own actions because true creation requires detailed knowledge, which humans lack.

Core Idea
A creator must know what he creates, but we don't know the details of our own actions.

The fourth proof against human creation is a logical syllogism: If we created our actions, we would know them; we do not; therefore we do not create them. Sanusi supports this with both Quranic verse and rational argument, showing that intention requires knowledge of the act's details.

Guided Path
1
Understand the overall argument
Read the passage and identify the conditional syllogism: If servant creates, he knows details; but he does not know details; therefore he does not create.
2
Examine the first premise: creator must know
Look at the Quranic evidence and the rational argument: choice requires intention, intention requires knowledge.
3
Examine the second premise: servant does not know
Consider the proofs given: the sleeping and distracted person perform actions without awareness of details; the body movement example starts here.
The passage is cut off at the end, but the first two proofs are clear.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Combine both premises to reach the conclusion: the servant is not the creator (mūjid) of his actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البرهان الرابع لو كان العبد موجداً لأفعال نفسه، لكان عالماً بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه وهو غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه، فوجب أن لا يكون موجداً لأفعال نفسه فنفتقر ههنا إلى إثبات مقدمتين: أما المقدمة الأولى: وهي قولنا: لو كان موجداً لأفعال نفسه، لكان عالماً بتفاصيل نفسه فيدل عليه القرآن والبرهان أما القرآن: فهو قوله: (ألا يعلم من خلق)؟ استكبر أن يكون الخالق للشيء، غير عالم به وأما البرهان: فهو إن العبد يمكنه ان يأتي بالأزيد مما أتى به، وبالأنقص عما أتى به، وبفعل آخر مغاير لما أتى به. فلما كان قادراً على الكل، كان رجحان بعض هذه الممكنات على البعض، لا بد أن يكون لأجل أن القادر المختار: خصص ذلك النوع، وذلك المقدار بالوقوع. دون المغاير، ودون الأزيد والأنقص. لكن القصد إلى إيقاع الشيء بقدر خاص، وكيفية خاص مشروط بالعلم بذلك القدر. لأن القصد إلى الشيء، بدون الشعور بماهيته: محال. فثبت: أن خالق الشيء لا بد وأن يكون قاصداً إليه، وثبت: أن القاصد إلى الشيء عالم بماهية ذلك الشيء، الذي قصد إليه. وذلك يدل: على أن خالق الشيء، لا بد وأن يكون عالماً به وأما المقدمة الثانية: وهي قولنا: إن العبد غير عالم بتفاصيل أفعال نفسه. فيدل عليه وجوه: الأول: إن النائم والساهي قد يصدر عنهم كثير من الأفعال الاختيارية، مع أنه لا شعور لهم بتفاصيل تلك الأفعال لا بكميتها ولا بكيفيتها الثاني: إن الإنسان إذا حرك بدنه وجثته، فلا شك أن بدنه مؤلف
The Fourth Proof: If the servant were the creator (mūjid) of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of his actions, but he is not knowledgeable of the details of his actions, therefore he must not be the creator of his actions. We need here to establish two premises: As for the first premise—that is our statement: If he were the creator of his own actions, he would be knowledgeable of the details of his own actions. The Quran and rational proof indicate it. As for the Quran: it is His saying: 'Does He who created not know?' He deemed it great that the creator of a thing be ignorant of it. As for the rational proof: indeed the servant is able to bring about more than he did, and less than he did, and another act different from what he did. Since he is capable of all, the preponderance of some of these possibilities over others must be because the freely choosing agent (al-qādir al-mukhtār) specified that type and that measure for occurrence, excluding the different, the greater, and the lesser. But the intention (qaṣd) to bring about something in a specific measure and specific modality is conditioned upon knowledge of that measure, because intending something without awareness of its quiddity (māhiyya) is impossible. Thus it is established that the creator of a thing must intend it, and it is established that the one who intends something is knowledgeable of the quiddity of that thing which he intended. And that indicates that the creator of a thing must be knowledgeable of it. As for the second premise—our statement: that the servant is not knowledgeable of the details of his own actions. Several aspects indicate it: First: The sleeping and the distracted person may perform many voluntary actions, yet they have no awareness of the details of those actions—neither their quantity nor their quality. Second: When a person moves his body and torso, there is no doubt that his body is composed...
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof (burhān) against the idea that a servant creates his own actions. The proof is structured as a conditional syllogism with two premises. The overall argument: If the servant were the creator of his actions, he would know their details; but he does not know the details; therefore he is not the creator. The author then undertakes to establish both premises. For the first premise (creator must know), he gives two pieces of evidence: the Quranic verse 'Does He who created not know?' (Sūrat al-Mulk, 67:14), and a rational argument. The rational argument: The servant can do more, less, or different actions; the fact that he does a specific act in a specific way requires that he intend it; intention requires knowledge of the act's quiddity (māhiyya) and measure; therefore a creator must know what he creates. For the second premise (servant does not know details), two proofs are given (the third is cut off in the text): (1) People sometimes perform voluntary actions while asleep or distracted, without being aware of the details (quantity or quality) of those actions. (2) When a person moves his body, he is not fully aware of how the body parts compose and move (this proof is incomplete here).

Key Terms
موجد
أفعال العبد
علم بتفاصيل
قصد
قادر مختار
شعور
ماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof only applies to complex or deliberate actions, not simple voluntary actions.
Correction: The proof applies to all voluntary actions, even simple ones like moving a finger, because any specific act requires intention and hence knowledge of its details.

Checkpoint
What Quranic verse is used to support the first premise (that a creator must know his creation)?
A) 'وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون'
B) 'ألا يعلم من خلق'
C) 'الله خالق كل شيء'
D) 'إن الله بكل شيء عليم'

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof demonstrates that human lack of detailed knowledge of their own voluntary actions proves they cannot be their creators.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of an action you performed today that you thought you fully controlled. Can you honestly say you knew every detail of how your body moved to accomplish it? How does this realization humble you before Allah's complete knowledge?
?
If you cannot even be fully aware of your own voluntary actions, how can you claim any independence from Allah's will? What would change in your daily life if you truly believed that every breath you take is created by Allah in full detail?
?
The proof shows that intention requires knowledge. How many times have you intended to do something for Allah but lacked knowledge of how to do it properly? Does this motivate you to seek more knowledge before acting?

Jabriyya's Determinism Implies God Is Necessary, Not Free
Author's second added objection: Jabriyya's determinism entails God is necessary, not willful.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection against the Jabriyya: that their view of necessary causation leads to God being a necessary agent rather than a free agent by choice, and the counter-argument that this leads to absurdity.

Core Idea
If actions are necessitated by power and motive, then God too is a necessary cause.

The author presents another powerful objection against the determinist (Jabriyya) position. He argues that if human actions are necessarily produced when power and motive are present, then the same logic applies to God: He would be a necessary agent, not a free agent who acts by will. The author then hints at the standard response, showing how the objection actually undermines the Jabriyya's own position.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage silently, then the literal translation. Notice the logical flow: 'If...then...' structure.
The passage contains a second objection and a brief response.
2
Identify the key claim of the Jabriyya
According to the author, the Jabriyya hold that an act necessarily occurs when power and motive are present, and is impossible otherwise.
This is the premise that leads to the conclusion.
3
Understand the implication for God
The author argues that if acts are necessary given their causes, then God's actions become necessitated, making Him a necessary agent (mūjib bi al-dhāt) rather than a free agent (fā‘il bi al-ikhtiyār).
This is the main problem pointed out.
4
Examine the counter-argument
The author mentions that the Jabriyya could respond, but if their view leads to God being necessary, then it also leads to denying any effective causality and allowing something to happen without a cause – which is absurd.
Notice the passage ends abruptly; the full argument is not given.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثاني : إن مذهب الجبرية : أن حصول الفعل عند مجموع القدرة والداعي : واجب . وحصوله عند فقدان هذا المجموع : ممتنع . وهذا يقتضي كونه تعالى موجباً بالذات ، لا فاعلا بالاختيار .
واعلم : أن الجواب المعتمد عن الوجه الثاني : إنا بينا فيما تقدم : أنه إن لزم على مذهب [ الجبرية) ] القول بأن الصانع موجب بالذات ، لا فاعل بالاختيار ، لزمهم على مذهبهم : نفي المؤثر بالكلية ، وتجويز أن يترجح أحد (1) من (م ، ل ) .
The second aspect: Indeed, the doctrine of the Jabriyya [determinists] is that the occurrence of the act at the conjunction of power and motive is necessary, and its occurrence in the absence of this conjunction is impossible. And this entails that He, exalted, is a necessary being by essence (mūjib bi al-dhāt), not a free agent by choice (fā‘il bi al-ikhtiyār). And know that the relied-upon answer regarding the second aspect: We have shown earlier that if it follows from the doctrine of the Jabriyya to say that the Maker is necessary by essence, not a free agent by choice, then it would follow from their doctrine the negation of any effect entirely, and the allowance that one [possible] is preferred without a preferrer.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage presents the author's second original objection against those who deny that the servant creates his own actions (i.e., the Jabriyya). The author argues that if the occurrence of an action is necessarily linked to the presence of both power (qudra) and motive (dā‘ī), then actions are compelled, not freely chosen. This implies that God, as the ultimate agent, is also a necessary agent (mūjib bi al-dhāt) like a natural cause, rather than a free agent (fā‘il bi al-ikhtiyār) who acts by choice. The author then mentions the standard answer to this objection: If the Jabriyya's view leads to God being a necessary agent, then it would also lead to the absurdity of denying any effective cause at all, and would allow a possible thing to be preferred without a preferrer—which amounts to a contradiction. The response is cut off but clearly intends to show that the objection backfires on the Jabriyya.

Correction: The author shows that the same logic applies to God: if acts are necessary when their causes are complete, then God's actions are also necessitated, making Him a necessary agent rather than a free agent.

Key Takeaway
The Jabriyya's necessary causation implies God is a necessary agent, contradicting His free will; and the objection backfires by leading to absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Jabariyya Implies God is Necessary by Essence
The author presents the second objection: jabariyya implies God is necessary by essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the jabariyya view of action leads to the conclusion that God is a necessary agent rather than a free agent.

Core Idea
Jabariyya determinism reduces God to a necessary cause, not a free chooser.

The author now presents a second objection against the jabariyya: their deterministic model of action implies that God is not a voluntary agent but a necessary one. This passage defines their position and draws out its theological consequence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the two-part structure: definition then implication.
2
Identify the two claims of jabariyya
The passage states: when power and motive are combined, the act is necessary; when they are absent, the act is impossible. Understand this deterministic framework.
This is the core of jabariyya doctrine.
3
Understand the implication for God
The author argues that this deterministic view makes God an 'agent by essence' (muujib bi al-dhaat) like fire, not a free agent (faa'il bi al-ikhtiyaar). Reflect on why this is theologically problematic.
This highlights the conflict between determinism and divine free will.

Refuting the Impossibility of a Miracle After a Liar
Refutes the opponent's claim by showing impossibility cannot arise from power or motivation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the opponent's claim that a miracle cannot occur after a liar's statement by analyzing the two possible sources of impossibility: power and motivation.

Core Idea
A possible act under a powerful God cannot be impossible—neither by power nor by motivation.

This passage presents a concise refutation of a key objection against the possibility of miracles. The opponent argued that if a liar claims prophethood, God cannot subsequently create a miracle because that would validate the lie. The author dismantles this by showing that the act itself is possible, God's power extends to all possibles, and the opponent's own principles prevent them from citing motivation as a barrier. Let's examine the logical structure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim
Read the first sentence to see what is being refuted: the opponent says God cannot create a miracle after a liar's claim.
2
Analyze the power argument
Notice the reasoning: the act (splitting the moon) is possible in itself, and God is powerful over all possible things. Therefore, impossibility cannot stem from a lack of power.
The author uses the example of splitting the moon as a possible act.
3
Analyze the motivation argument
Understand why motivation cannot be the source: because the opponent's own view holds that the ugliness of an action does not affect God's motivation. Thus, impossibility cannot be due to lack of motivation.
This argument uses the opponent's own principles against them.
4
Synthesize the conclusion
Combine both parts: since impossibility cannot be attributed to either power or motivation, the opponent's claim that such an event is impossible is definitively false.
The conclusion is that the opponent's statement is 'bāṭil qaṭʿan' (definitively false).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : وهو أن قولكم : إنه تعالى لا يصح منه خلق المعجز عقيب دعوى الكاذب : كلام باطل . لأن فلق القمر ، عقيب تكلم إنسان بكلام كذب ، ممكن في نفسه . والله تعالى قادر على كل الممكنات ، فيمتنع حصول هذا الامتناع، نظرا إلى القدرة ، ويمتنع أيضاً حصوله نظراً إلى الداعي . لأن قبح القبائح ، لا تأثير لها عندكم في هذا الباب . ولما ثبت أنه لا يمكن القول بحصول هذا الامتناع . لا نظراً إلى القدرة ، ولا نظراً إلى الإرادة والداعي. كان القول بثبوت هذا الامتناع : باطلاً قطعاً
The fourth: And it is that your statement: Indeed, it is not valid for Him, exalted, to create a miracle after the claim of a liar is false speech. Because the splitting of the moon after a human speaks false speech is possible in itself. And God, exalted, is powerful over all possible things. So this impossibility cannot occur with respect to power, and also cannot occur with respect to motivation. Because the ugliness of ugly actions has no effect, according to you, in this matter. And when it is established that it is not possible to say that this impossibility occurs, neither with respect to power nor with respect to will and motivation, then the statement that this impossibility is established is definitively false.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a fourth argument refuting the opponent's claim that God cannot create a miracle after a liar's claim. The author states that the opponent's statement is false because splitting the moon after a false speech is possible in itself, and God is powerful over all possible things. Therefore, the impossibility of such an event cannot be due to lack of power. It also cannot be due to lack of motivation, because the opponent's own position holds that the ugliness of an action does not affect God's motivation. Since the impossibility cannot be attributed to either power or motivation, the claim that it is impossible is definitively false.

Key Takeaway

If God Can Create Evil, He Can Lie
First argument: God's creating evil implies He can lie.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the premise that God can create evil leads to the possibility of Him lying, thereby undermining the Qur'an as a proof.

Core Idea
If evil is possible from God, then lying is too.

The author begins by stating the first of three reasons why denying human agency makes the Qur'an unreliable as a proof. The argument is straightforward: if God can create moral evil without it being considered ugly, then lying is not beneath Him either. This possibility alone strips the Qur'an of its evidential force, because it could be false. The passage then anticipates an objection from those who believe God's speech is an eternal attribute that cannot be false.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the first part of the passage where the author presents the core argument: since God can create evil, He can lie, so the Qur'an is not a proof.
2
Note the objection
Identify the objection that God's speech is an eternal attribute and thus cannot be false.
The objection is introduced with 'لا يقال'.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why the possibility of lying destroys the Qur'an's status as a proof. What would be needed for certainty?
This sets up the need for a refutation, which comes in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان أن القول بأن العبد غير موجد لأفعال نفسه ، ينافي الإقرار يكون القرآن حجة : فبيانه من ثلاثة أوجه : الأول : إنه لما لم يقبح منه تعالى ، خلق الضلالات والفواحش . فكيف يقبح منه أن يكذب ؟ ومع هذا التجويز لا يبقى القرآن حجة . لا يقال كلام الله صفة قديمة، والصفة القديمة يمتنع أن تكون كذباً . لأنا نقول : إن هذا الكلام : باطل من وجوه : الأول : إنا لا نسلم أن كلام الله صفة قديمة. فإن ذلك مما عظم الخلاف فيه، بيننا وبينكم ثم نقول : لو كان كلام الله قديماً، لكان كذباً . والدليل عليه : أنه مشتمل على الإخبار عن الأمور الماضية .. كقوله تعالى : ( إنا أنزلناه في ليلة القدر ) - ( إنا أرسلنا نوحاً إلى قومه ) والإخبار عن الأمور الماضية لا يكون صدقاً إلا إذا كان المخبر عنه سابقا على الخبر . وكون الأدني مسبوقاً بغيره : محال · فثبت بهذا : أن كلام الله تعالي ، لو كان قديماً ، لكان كذباً . وأنتم ادعيتم أن كونه قديما ، ينافي كونه كاذباً . فوجب أن يقال : إن كونه قديماً ، ينافي كونه كلباً . قالوا : الدليل عليه : هو أنه تعالى عالم بجميع المعلومات ، وكل من كان عالماً بشيء ، لم يمتنع أن يخبر في نفسه ، عن ذلك الشيء بخبر صدق . فلو كان [ صدقه ] تعالي كذباً ، لكان ذلك الكذب قديماً ، والقديم يمتنع زواله . وإذا امتنع زوال الكذب ، امتنع حصول الصدق . لأن اجتماع الضدين : محال . فثبت : أنه تعالى ، لو كان كاذباً ، لامتنع عليه أن يخبر عما علمه بخبر صدق ، وقلنا : إن هذا الامتناع باطل ، فثبت : أن كلام الله صدق . واعلم : أن هذا الكلام ضعيف . لأنا نقول : كما أن العالم بالشيء يمكنه أن يخبر في نفسه عما علمه بخير صدق ، فكذلك يمكنه أيضاً أن يخبر [ عنه بخبر ] كذب ، وكون الكلام القديم صدقاً ، يمنع من إمكان هذا الكذب . فإن منعوا هذا الإمكان في جانب الكذب، منعناه أيضا في جانب الصدق . ثم لئن سلمنا : أن الكلام القديم يجب كونه صدقاً ، إلا أنكم لما تمسكتم بآيات القرآن على أنه تعالى هو الموجد لأعمال العباد ، فأنتم ما تمسكتم بذلك الكلام ، القديم الأزلي المنزه عن أن يكون حرفاً أو صوتاً. وإنما تمسكتم بهذه الألفاظ المركبة المحدثة المسموعة . فهب أن ذلك الكلام القديم : صدق ، إلا أن نقول : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن هذه الألفاظ التي نسمعها ، ونستدل بها في هذه المسألة ، تكون كلها أكاذيب وأضاليل وأباطيل ؟ فثبت : أنه وإن كان الكلام القديم صدقاً ، إلا أن ذلك لا ينفع في القطع بصحة مدلولات هذه الألفاظ التي نسمعها . وإن خلط أحد البابين بالآخر ، إما جهل أو تجاهل
And as for the explanation that the statement that the servant is not the creator of his own actions contradicts the acknowledgment that the Qur'an is a proof: its explanation is from three aspects. The first: Since it is not deemed ugly by Him, exalted is He, to create misguidance and indecencies, then how can it be deemed ugly for Him to lie? And with this possibility, the Qur'an does not remain a proof. It cannot be said: 'The speech of Allah is an eternal attribute, and the eternal attribute is impossible to be a lie.' For we say: This statement is false in several aspects. The first: We do not concede that the speech of Allah is an eternal attribute, for that is a matter of great disagreement between us and you. Then we say: If the speech of Allah were eternal, it would be a lie. And the proof of it is that it contains information about past matters, like His saying: 'Indeed, We sent it down on the Night of Decree' and 'Indeed, We sent Noah to his people.' And information about past matters is not truthful unless the thing informed about is prior to the report. And for the latter [the report] to be preceded by something else is impossible. So it is established by this that the speech of Allah, if it were eternal, would be a lie. And you claimed that its being eternal precludes it being false. So it must be said that its being eternal is incompatible with it being false. They said: The proof of it is that He, exalted is He, is knower of all known things, and whoever is knower of a thing, it is not impossible for him to report in himself about that thing with a truthful report. So if His truth were false, that falsehood would be eternal, and the eternal is impossible to cease. And if ceasing of falsehood is impossible, then attaining truth is impossible, because the concurrence of two opposites is impossible. So it is established that He, exalted is He, if He were false, it would be impossible for Him to report about what He knows with a truthful report. And we say: This impossibility is false, so it is established that the speech of Allah is true. And know: This argument is weak. For we say: Just as the knower of a thing is able to report in himself about what he knows with a truthful report, so too is he able to report about it with a false report. And the fact that the eternal speech is true precludes the possibility of this falsehood. If they deny this possibility on the side of falsehood, we also deny it on the side of truth. Then even if we grant that the eternal speech must be true, nevertheless, since you have clung to the verses of the Qur'an that Allah is the creator of the actions of servants, you have not clung to that eternal, timeless speech that is free from being a letter or a sound. Rather, you have clung to these composite, originated, audible words. Suppose that eternal speech is true; yet we say: Why is it not permissible to say that these words which we hear and use as evidence in this issue are all lies, deceptions, and falsehoods? So it is established that even if the eternal speech is true, that does not help in certainty about the correctness of the connotations of these words that we hear. To mix the two matters is either ignorance or feigned ignorance.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is the first of three aspects demonstrating that the denial of human agency (the servant not being the creator of his own actions) contradicts the claim that the Qur'an is a definitive proof (hujja). The author argues as follows: First, if God can create misguidance and foul acts without it being deemed bad (qabih) by Him, then why cannot He lie? If lying is possible for God, then the Qur'an cannot be relied upon as proof. The opponent might object that God's speech is an eternal attribute, and an eternal attribute cannot be false. The author refutes this in several ways: (a) They do not concede that God's speech is eternal—this is disputed. (b) Even if it were eternal, it would be false because eternal speech informing of past events would require the events to be simultaneous with speech, but past events are prior, so the speech would be false. The opponents then argue that since God is all-knowing, He can only tell the truth, and if He lied, that falsehood would be eternal and could not be replaced by truth. The author dismisses this as weak: just as a knower can tell truth, he can also lie—eternal truth does not preclude the possibility of eternal falsehood. If they deny that possibility, symmetry demands denial on both sides. Even conceding that eternal speech must be true, the author points out that the opponents rely on the audible, composite words of the Qur'an, not the eternal attribute. These words could be false even if the eternal is true. Thus, the argument does not secure certainty.

Key Terms
موجد
حجة
قبح
قديم
صفة قديمة
كذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God's speech is eternal, it cannot be false, so the Qur'an is automatically true.
Correction: The author will later argue that eternity does not guarantee truth; an eternal statement about past events would actually be false, and even if the eternal speech is true, the audible Qur'an could still be false.

Checkpoint
What is the author's first argument against the Qur'an being a proof?
A) The Qur'an contains contradictions.
B) If God can create evil, He can lie, so the Qur'an could be false.
C) The Qur'an is not from God.
D) Human actions are not created by God.

Key Takeaway
The possibility of God lying, given His creation of evil, undermines the Qur'an's certainty as a proof.

?
The author uses logic to defend the Qur'an's authority. Have you built your certainty in revelation on rational foundations, or does your faith rest merely on upbringing? What would happen if a doubt about God's truthfulness entered your mind?

Refuting the Eternity of Speech
Two refutations of the objection that God's speech is eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two refutations of the claim that God's speech is eternal and therefore cannot be false: (1) the disagreement over its eternity, and (2) the argument that if it were eternal it would actually be false.

Core Idea
Eternal speech about past events would be false.

The author now responds to the objection that God's speech is an eternal attribute and thus cannot be false. He provides two counterpoints: first, the claim that speech is eternal is not universally accepted; second, even if it were eternal, it would be false because it speaks about past events that are temporally prior. This lesson unpacks these refutations.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation
Read the passage starting from 'لأنا نقول' up to 'فوجب أن يقال' to see both counterarguments.
2
Understand the first counter
The first point: we do not concede that speech is an eternal attribute; there is great disagreement on this matter between us and you (the opponents).
3
Analyze the second counter
The second point: even if it were eternal, it would be a lie, because it reports on past events that are prior to the report, which is impossible for an eternal being.
The author uses examples from the Qur'an like 'We sent it down on the Night of Decree' to illustrate.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Notice how the author concludes that the opponents' claim that eternity precludes falsehood is defeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان أن القول بأن العبد غير موجد لأفعال نفسه ، ينافي الإقرار يكون القرآن حجة : فبيانه من ثلاثة أوجه : الأول : إنه لما لم يقبح منه تعالى ، خلق الضلالات والفواحش . فكيف يقبح منه أن يكذب ؟ ومع هذا التجويز لا يبقى القرآن حجة . لا يقال كلام الله صفة قديمة، والصفة القديمة يمتنع أن تكون كذباً . لأنا نقول : إن هذا الكلام : باطل من وجوه : الأول : إنا لا نسلم أن كلام الله صفة قديمة. فإن ذلك مما عظم الخلاف فيه، بيننا وبينكم ثم نقول : لو كان كلام الله قديماً، لكان كذباً . والدليل عليه : أنه مشتمل على الإخبار عن الأمور الماضية .. كقوله تعالى : ( إنا أنزلناه في ليلة القدر ) - ( إنا أرسلنا نوحاً إلى قومه ) والإخبار عن الأمور الماضية لا يكون صدقاً إلا إذا كان المخبر عنه سابقا على الخبر . وكون الأدني مسبوقاً بغيره : محال · فثبت بهذا : أن كلام الله تعالي ، لو كان قديماً ، لكان كذباً . وأنتم ادعيتم أن كونه قديما ، ينافي كونه كاذباً . فوجب أن يقال : إن كونه قديماً ، ينافي كونه كلباً . قالوا : الدليل عليه : هو أنه تعالى عالم بجميع المعلومات ، وكل من كان عالماً بشيء ، لم يمتنع أن يخبر في نفسه ، عن ذلك الشيء بخبر صدق . فلو كان [ صدقه ] تعالي كذباً ، لكان ذلك الكذب قديماً ، والقديم يمتنع زواله . وإذا امتنع زوال الكذب ، امتنع حصول الصدق . لأن اجتماع الضدين : محال . فثبت : أنه تعالى ، لو كان كاذباً ، لامتنع عليه أن يخبر عما علمه بخبر صدق ، وقلنا : إن هذا الامتناع باطل ، فثبت : أن كلام الله صدق . واعلم : أن هذا الكلام ضعيف . لأنا نقول : كما أن العالم بالشيء يمكنه أن يخبر في نفسه عما علمه بخير صدق ، فكذلك يمكنه أيضاً أن يخبر [ عنه بخبر ] كذب ، وكون الكلام القديم صدقاً ، يمنع من إمكان هذا الكذب . فإن منعوا هذا الإمكان في جانب الكذب، منعناه أيضا في جانب الصدق . ثم لئن سلمنا : أن الكلام القديم يجب كونه صدقاً ، إلا أنكم لما تمسكتم بآيات القرآن على أنه تعالى هو الموجد لأعمال العباد ، فأنتم ما تمسكتم بذلك الكلام ، القديم الأزلي المنزه عن أن يكون حرفاً أو صوتاً. وإنما تمسكتم بهذه الألفاظ المركبة المحدثة المسموعة . فهب أن ذلك الكلام القديم : صدق ، إلا أن نقول : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إن هذه الألفاظ التي نسمعها ، ونستدل بها في هذه المسألة ، تكون كلها أكاذيب وأضاليل وأباطيل ؟ فثبت : أنه وإن كان الكلام القديم صدقاً ، إلا أن ذلك لا ينفع في القطع بصحة مدلولات هذه الألفاظ التي نسمعها . وإن خلط أحد البابين بالآخر ، إما جهل أو تجاهل
And as for the explanation that the statement that the servant is not the creator of his own actions contradicts the acknowledgment that the Qur'an is a proof: its explanation is from three aspects. The first: Since it is not deemed ugly by Him, exalted is He, to create misguidance and indecencies, then how can it be deemed ugly for Him to lie? And with this possibility, the Qur'an does not remain a proof. It cannot be said: 'The speech of Allah is an eternal attribute, and the eternal attribute is impossible to be a lie.' For we say: This statement is false in several aspects. The first: We do not concede that the speech of Allah is an eternal attribute, for that is a matter of great disagreement between us and you. Then we say: If the speech of Allah were eternal, it would be a lie. And the proof of it is that it contains information about past matters, like His saying: 'Indeed, We sent it down on the Night of Decree' and 'Indeed, We sent Noah to his people.' And information about past matters is not truthful unless the thing informed about is prior to the report. And for the latter [the report] to be preceded by something else is impossible. So it is established by this that the speech of Allah, if it were eternal, would be a lie. And you claimed that its being eternal precludes it being false. So it must be said that its being eternal is incompatible with it being false. They said: The proof of it is that He, exalted is He, is knower of all known things, and whoever is knower of a thing, it is not impossible for him to report in himself about that thing with a truthful report. So if His truth were false, that falsehood would be eternal, and the eternal is impossible to cease. And if ceasing of falsehood is impossible, then attaining truth is impossible, because the concurrence of two opposites is impossible. So it is established that He, exalted is He, if He were false, it would be impossible for Him to report about what He knows with a truthful report. And we say: This impossibility is false, so it is established that the speech of Allah is true. And know: This argument is weak. For we say: Just as the knower of a thing is able to report in himself about what he knows with a truthful report, so too is he able to report about it with a false report. And the fact that the eternal speech is true precludes the possibility of this falsehood. If they deny this possibility on the side of falsehood, we also deny it on the side of truth. Then even if we grant that the eternal speech must be true, nevertheless, since you have clung to the verses of the Qur'an that Allah is the creator of the actions of servants, you have not clung to that eternal, timeless speech that is free from being a letter or a sound. Rather, you have clung to these composite, originated, audible words. Suppose that eternal speech is true; yet we say: Why is it not permissible to say that these words which we hear and use as evidence in this issue are all lies, deceptions, and falsehoods? So it is established that even if the eternal speech is true, that does not help in certainty about the correctness of the connotations of these words that we hear. To mix the two matters is either ignorance or feigned ignorance.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is the first of three aspects demonstrating that the denial of human agency (the servant not being the creator of his own actions) contradicts the claim that the Qur'an is a definitive proof (hujja). The author argues as follows: First, if God can create misguidance and foul acts without it being deemed bad (qabih) by Him, then why cannot He lie? If lying is possible for God, then the Qur'an cannot be relied upon as proof. The opponent might object that God's speech is an eternal attribute, and an eternal attribute cannot be false. The author refutes this in several ways: (a) They do not concede that God's speech is eternal—this is disputed. (b) Even if it were eternal, it would be false because eternal speech informing of past events would require the events to be simultaneous with speech, but past events are prior, so the speech would be false. The opponents then argue that since God is all-knowing, He can only tell the truth, and if He lied, that falsehood would be eternal and could not be replaced by truth. The author dismisses this as weak: just as a knower can tell truth, he can also lie—eternal truth does not preclude the possibility of eternal falsehood. If they deny that possibility, symmetry demands denial on both sides. Even conceding that eternal speech must be true, the author points out that the opponents rely on the audible, composite words of the Qur'an, not the eternal attribute. These words could be false even if the eternal is true. Thus, the argument does not secure certainty.

قديم
صفة قديمة
كذب
صدق
ماض

Checkpoint
What is the second refutation given by the author against the claim that eternal speech cannot be false?
A) Eternal speech is impossible.
B) If speech were eternal, it would be false because it reports past events that are prior.
C) The Qur'an is not eternal.
D) God cannot lie.

Key Takeaway
Even if speech were eternal, that does not guarantee its truth; it could actually be false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that everything about Allah is perfect, how does it feel to realize that believing His speech is eternal could actually make it false? Are you willing to re-examine your assumptions even if they are widely held?
?
This argument uses simple logic to challenge a deeply held theological position. Have you ever held a belief about God that, upon honest reflection, you realized was logically inconsistent? What did you do about it?
?
The author does not simply reject the opponent's view; he turns their own premise against them. When you defend your beliefs, do you prepare to face such rigorous logical scrutiny, or do you rely on emotional comfort? Will you commit today to testing every belief about Allah with the same logical rigor?

The Weakness of the Eternal Truth Argument
Dismissal of the opponent's proof and final distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opponent's counter-argument that God's knowledge ensures truth, the author's dismissal of it as weak, and the final point that the audible Qur'an could still be false even if the eternal speech is true.

Core Idea
Even if eternal speech is true, the words we hear may be false.

The opponents respond by arguing that since God is all-knowing, He can only tell the truth, and if He lied it would be eternal and never change, making truth impossible. The author dismisses this as weak, noting symmetry: if truth precludes falsehood, then falsehood precludes truth. More importantly, he makes a decisive point: even if the eternal speech is true, the audible words of the Qur'an that we rely on are not that eternal speech; they could be false. Thus, the argument does not secure certainty.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's counter-argument
Read from 'قالوا : الدليل عليه' to understand their claim that God's knowledge necessitates truth and that falsehood would be eternal and prevent truth.
2
Read the author's dismissal
Read 'واعلم أن هذا الكلام ضعيف' to see why the author considers it weak.
The author uses a symmetry argument.
3
Grasp the final point
Read the last part about the distinction between eternal speech and audible words, noting that even if eternal is true, the words we hear could be false.
This is the key conclusion against the opponent's position.

The Proof and Refutation of Divine Speech's Truthfulness
Author presents and then refutes the argument that God's speech must be truthful.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam argument for the truthfulness of God's speech based on omniscience and the critique that it does not secure the reliability of the recited Qur'an.

Core Idea
A proof from omniscience can be turned around, and the recited words are not the eternal speech.

This lesson examines a key argument in kalam about the nature of God's speech. The author first presents the proof that God's speech must be true because He is omniscient, then reveals its weakness by showing it can be reversed and that the recited Qur'an is created and possibly false. You will see how theological reasoning can be both constructed and deconstructed.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation, to grasp the overall flow. Notice the structure: first a proof, then a refutation.
The passage begins with 'قالوا' (they said) indicating an opponent's argument.
2
Analyze the proof
Identify the steps of the proof: from God's omniscience to the necessity of truthful speech, and the claim that if falsehood were eternal, truth could never occur.
The key assumption is that eternal falsehood cannot cease, so truth cannot arise.
3
Examine the refutation
See how the author counters: the same reasoning allows false reports, and even if eternal speech is true, the audible words are created and could be false.
The author distinguishes between eternal speech (muthbat) and created words (muhdath).
4
Reflect on implications
Consider why this matters: the argument was used to defend Qur'anic inerrancy, but the refutation shows it does not guarantee the reliability of the recited text.
Mixing the two domains is a fallacy.
